Solo hoped to use the archive to get several people they owed money to off their backs. Solo, posing as a First Order officer, boarded Mek Nu'Tiv's cruiser and spoke with her and her crew. Nu'Tiv, however, realized that Solo had used Finwej to get credits and had her crew hold him at gunpoint.[[170]](#cite_note-PD_annual_2-170)

#### Retaking the *Falcon*[]

:   "*The Jedi were real?*"  
    "*I used to wonder about that myself. Thought it was a bunch of mumbo jumbo. A magical power holding together good and evil, the dark side and the light. Crazy thing is, it's true. The Force, the Jedi. All of it—it's all true.*"
:   ―Rey and Han Solo[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

 [![Solo pleased to be back aboard the Falcon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/HanIsHome-TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416065319) [![Solo pleased to be back aboard the Falcon](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/HanIsHome-TFA.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/270?cb=20160416065319)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/HanIsHome-TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416065319) 

Solo pleased to be back aboard the *Falcon*

 

In [34 ABY](/wiki/34_ABY "34 ABY")[[169]](#cite_note-Date1-169) while transporting a cargo of three Rathtars aboard the *Eravana* for the King [Prana](/wiki/Grevoth_Prana_IX "Grevoth Prana IX"), Han and Chewie found the *Falcon* floating in space near the desert planet of Jakku, pulling his prized vessel in with a tractor beam. Upon boarding their old vessel, the two went about inspecting their ship and found two stowaways, Jakku scavenger [Rey](/wiki/Rey_Skywalker "Rey Skywalker") and former First Order [stormtrooper](/wiki/First_Order_stormtrooper "First Order stormtrooper") [Finn](/wiki/Finn "Finn"), who he assumed were the thieves who had stolen the *Falcon*. When Rey and Finn explained that they were going to take a droid named [BB-8](/wiki/BB-8 "BB-8") to the Resistance as he had a map to the location of Solo's old friend Luke Skywalker, Han and Chewie agreed to help them.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

Solo rediscovered the *[Smuggler's Guide](/wiki/Smuggler%27s_Guide "Smuggler's Guide")* that was previously owned by [Unkar Plutt](/wiki/Unkar_Plutt "Unkar Plutt") aboard the ship, thinking it was a bad omen that this thing keeps resurfacing. However, Chewbacca thought it was a good luck that it keeps coming back and was happy to see the logbook and kept opening different pages. Han thought if that was true his life would have turned out differently. These reflections were recorded in the logbook.[[171]](#cite_note-Smuggler's_Guide-171)

#### Skirmish aboard the *Eravana*[]

:   "*What are you going to do?*"  
    "*Same thing I always do, talk my way out of it.*"
:   ―Rey and Han Solo[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

 [![Han Solo trapped between two criminal factions aboard the Eravana](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/Long_Con_SoR.png/revision/latest?cb=20190311043543) [![Han Solo trapped between two criminal factions aboard the Eravana](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/Long_Con_SoR.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20190311043543)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/Long_Con_SoR.png/revision/latest?cb=20190311043543) 

Han Solo trapped between two criminal factions aboard the *Eravana*

 

Han's freighter had been boarded by the Guavian Death Gang and Kanjiklub, whom Solo was indebted to. Not wanting Rey and Finn to be involved, Han placed both of them in the lower corridors of the freighter while he and Chewie went to meet with the criminals, with BB-8 accompanying them. The smuggler tried but failed to convince both gangs that he would fix things eventually, with one of the gang leaders threatening to take away the *Millennium Falcon* as payback. Han having just retrieved his vessel, responded that they would have to take it over his dead body. One of the criminals then recognized the BB-8 unit from a First Order bounty placed on it along with Rey and Finn, and demanded that Han hand over the droid and any stowaways he might have on board. Right before a firefight broke out, Rey accidentally released the rathtars, providing a diversion for an escape in the *Falcon*.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

#### Journey to Takodana[]

:   "*She's run this watering hole for a thousand years. Maz is a bit of an acquired taste, so let me do the talking. And whatever you do, don't stare.*"  
    "*At what?*"  
    "Any *of it.*"
:   ―Han Solo, Rey and Finn[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

 [![Han asks Maz Kanata to get BB-8 to the Resistance.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/MeetingWithMaz-TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416071837) [![Han asks Maz Kanata to get BB-8 to the Resistance.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/MeetingWithMaz-TFA.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/270?cb=20160416071837)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/MeetingWithMaz-TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416071837) 

Han asks Maz Kanata to get BB-8 to the Resistance.

 

Han explained that Luke tried to rebuild the Jedi Order, but an apprentice of his turned to the dark side and became Kylo Ren, destroying all that Luke had built, including the other [Padawans](/wiki/Padawan "Padawan") that Luke had trained. Feeling responsible and blaming himself for the failure, Luke went into exile.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

En route to Takodana, Han reminisced about the *Falcon*, her corridors, fresh smell of thread grease, stale funk of the couch fabric. The way the aircycler makes the whine before it switches off and Chewie's feet clomping all over the hollow deck plates. He thought about dropping the logbook off with Maz, but changed his mind. His thoughts were recorded in the *Smuggler's Guide*.[[171]](#cite_note-Smuggler's_Guide-171) Later on the same route, the *Falcon*'s hyperdrive cut out. Rey, Finn, and Chewbacca investigated and found a tracker near the [sensor pulse generator](/wiki/Sensor_pulse_generator "Sensor pulse generator"). Finn removed the tracker, only to discover that it was rigged with explosives. Rey and Chewie jettisoned the tracker bomb out the airlock, while Finn informed Han of the situation and the *Falcon* jumped back into hyperspace.[[172]](#cite_note-Tracker_Trouble-172)

##### Scoundrel's redemption[]

:   "*And maybe she could carry on after I'm gone. Another roll of a dice. A scoundrel's redemption.*"
:   ―Han Solo, in the *Smuggler's Guide*[[171]](#cite_note-Smuggler's_Guide-171)

 [![By the time they arrived on Takodana, Rey came to regard Solo as a mentor and father figure.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0d/Rey_and_Han_Solo.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20170115230944) [![By the time they arrived on Takodana, Rey came to regard Solo as a mentor and father figure.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0d/Rey_and_Han_Solo.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/260?cb=20170115230944)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0d/Rey_and_Han_Solo.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20170115230944) 

By the time they arrived on Takodana, Rey came to regard Solo as a mentor and father figure.

 

Solo handed Rey an [NN-14 blaster pistol](/wiki/NN-14_blaster_pistol "NN-14 blaster pistol"), knowing she would be able to defend herself with it, and asked Rey what her name was. With the two formally introduced, Solo said he was considering bringing on a new crew member. Impressed with Rey's piloting and repair abilities, he said he would consider offering her a job as a [second mate](/wiki/Second_mate "Second mate") aboard the *Falcon*. Rey was flattered by the offer and briefly excited by the prospect, but she turned it down because she had to return to Jakku to wait for her family, claiming that she'd already been away for too long already.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

##### Takodana Castle[]

Solo took Rey and Finn to meet his old friend Kanata at her castle. There, he learned that Kanata had found and kept the old lightsaber that once belonged to Luke, and he asked where Kanata got the weapon, but Kanata dismissed him, saying it was a story for another time. While there, the First Order was alerted to BB-8's presence and attacked. During the ensuing battle, he killed several stormtroopers both with his DL-44 blaster and [Chewbacca's](/wiki/Chewbacca%27s_bowcaster "Chewbacca's bowcaster") [bowcaster](/wiki/Bowcaster "Bowcaster"), Solo, Finn, and Chewbacca were initially captured, but escaped when the Resistance, also alerted to BB-8's presence, counterattacked. Despite the First Order being driven off, Han witnessed his son Kylo Ren carrying away Rey. Among his rescuers on Takodana was Han's estranged wife, General Leia Organa. She took Han, Chewbacca, Finn, and BB-8 to the Resistance [base](/wiki/Resistance_base "Resistance base") on [D'Qar](/wiki/D%27Qar "D'Qar").[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

#### Reunited at the Resistance base[]

:   "*If Luke couldn't reach him, how could I?"  
    "Luke is a Jedi, you're his father.*"
:   ―Han and Leia[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

 [![Organa embraces Solo](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e0/Han_and_Leia_hug_TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160122053600) [![Organa embraces Solo](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e0/Han_and_Leia_hug_TFA.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/245?cb=20160122053600)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e0/Han_and_Leia_hug_TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160122053600) 

Organa embraces Solo

 

It is revealed that Han and Leia are aware that their son is Kylo Ren, and that their son's fall to the dark side caused them to separate, with Han returning to his smuggling business, and Leia spearheading the activities of the New Republic and the Resistance. As Starkiller Base prepared to wipe out the world of D'Qar, the site of the Resistance's headquarters, the Resistance planned an [attack](/wiki/Battle_of_Starkiller_Base "Battle of Starkiller Base") of their own. Finn had given them the Base's blueprints, which revealed that the base drained the energy of the [sun](/wiki/Star "Star") in order to charge its superweapon, and that it required a [thermal oscillator](/wiki/Thermal_oscillator "Thermal oscillator"), which sustained the energy on the planet, that, if destroyed, would destabilize the planet's core and implode the Base. However, they would need to do it before the Base fully charged its weapon. Having experience in taking down superweapons' shield generators, Solo and Chewbacca volunteered to disable the shield. Before he left, Leia told Han to find their son, and convince him to reject the dark side and return to the [light](/wiki/Light_side_of_the_Force "Light side of the Force").[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

#### Battle of Starkiller Base and death[]

:   "*I'm being torn apart. I want to be free of this pain. And I know what I have to do, but I don't know if I have the strength to do it. Will you help me?"  
    "Yes. Anything.*"
:   ―Kylo Ren and Han Solo[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

 [![Han, Finn, and Chewbacca sneak into Starkiller Base to disable the shields.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/93/HanChewieFinn-TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416064751) [![Han, Finn, and Chewbacca sneak into Starkiller Base to disable the shields.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/93/HanChewieFinn-TFA.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/255?cb=20160416064751)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/93/HanChewieFinn-TFA.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416064751) 

Han, Finn, and Chewbacca sneak into Starkiller Base to disable the shields.

 

Solo, Finn, and Chewie took the *Millennium Falcon* to Starkiller Base, exiting hyperspace inside the planet's shield just above the surface and landing just at the side of a high cliff. When Finn revealed his stationing had previously been in "sanitation" and that the real reason he had come along was to rescue Rey from the First Order, Solo and Chewbacca agreed to help him with a bit of annoyance. While inside the base, they captured Captain [Phasma](/wiki/Phasma "Phasma") and forced her to lower the shields, after which Solo claimed that they would not leave the base without Rey.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4)

 [![Han is impaled by his own son's lightsaber.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/98/Kylo_kills_Solo.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416064307) [![Han is impaled by his own son's lightsaber.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/98/Kylo_kills_Solo.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/280?cb=20160416064307)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/98/Kylo_kills_Solo.png/revision/latest?cb=20160416064307) 

Han is impaled by his own son's lightsaber.

 

After finding Rey, the group headed to Starkiller Base's thermal oscillator to assist the Resistance pilots above in its destruction. While planting explosives with Chewbacca, Solo spotted Ren and confronted him on a long walkway positioned above a massive pit, where he attempted to convince his son to leave the First Order and come back with him. Ren handed his lightsaber to Solo, saying he was being "torn apart" and had one last thing to do. After a brief moment of emotional struggle, Ben activated the weapon and it passed through his own father's torso. As Rey, Finn, and Chewbacca watched in horror, Solo stroked his son's face for the last time before dying, his corpse falling over the side of the bridge and into the pit below. Leia sensed her husband's death through the Force and wept for his loss. Solo's death was later mourned by Organa, Chewbacca, and Rey when they returned to the Resistance Base from Starkiller Base after its destruction.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4) The [dwarf star](/wiki/Dwarf_star "Dwarf star") it exploded into was dubbed "[Solo](/wiki/Solo_(star) "Solo (star)")" in his honor.[[173]](#cite_note-TROSVD-173)

### Legacy[]

:   "*I know what I have to do, but I don't know if I have the strength to do it.*""*You do.*""*Dad…*""*I know.*"
:   ―Ben Solo and a memory of his father, Han Solo[[174]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-174)

Shortly after the battle, Leia asked Rey to tell her about how Solo died, as she only had sensed it. Rey told her that while she didn't hear what Solo told Ben, he didn't fight nor call out, to which Leia assured her that he always knew when to run and when to make a stand.[[175]](#cite_note-Age_of_Resistance_Rey-175) Sometime afterwards, a [funeral](/wiki/Funeral_of_Han_Solo "Funeral of Han Solo") was held for Solo.[[176]](#cite_note-The_Last_Jedi_Expanded_Edition-176) During the [evacuation of the D'Qar base](/wiki/Battle_of_D%27Qar "Battle of D'Qar"), one of the [proton bombs](/wiki/Proton_bomb "Proton bomb") carried by [Paige Tico](/wiki/Paige_Tico "Paige Tico")'s [bomber](/wiki/Bomber "Bomber"), *[Cobalt Hammer](/wiki/Cobalt_Hammer "Cobalt Hammer")*, succeeded in destroying Captain [Moden Canady](/wiki/Moden_Canady "Moden Canady")'s [*Mandator IV*-class Siege Dreadnought](/wiki/Mandator_IV-class_Siege_Dreadnought "Mandator IV-class Siege Dreadnought") *[Fulminatrix](/wiki/Fulminatrix "Fulminatrix")*. The ordnance crew had a message inscribed on the bomb in [Aurebesh](/wiki/Aurebesh "Aurebesh"), stating "Han says hi."[[177]](#cite_note-TLJVD-177)

After Solo's death, Rey, Chewbacca, and R2-D2 flew in the *Millennium Falcon* to the planet Ahch-To to recruit Jedi Master Luke Skywalker to the Resistance's cause while Kylo Ren recovered from the injuries he sustained during the Battle of Starkiller Base. As Skywalker [cut himself off](/wiki/Sever_Force "Sever Force") from the Force since he went into exile, he was unaware of what was happening in the galaxy, so he didn't feel Solo's death,[[177]](#cite_note-TLJVD-177) leading him to ask Rey and Chewie what had happened to his brother-in-law.[[178]](#cite_note-Episode_VIII-178) Upon becoming aware of Solo's fate, Skywalker regretted not having sensed it, leading Chewbacca to hug him before Rey asked him to train her.[[179]](#cite_note-TLJ_Adaptation_1-179)

To the mutual surprise of both Rey and Kylo, a [Force-bond](/wiki/Force-bond "Force-bond") had developed between them, psychically linking their [minds](/wiki/Brain "Brain") across the galaxy. The bond enabled them to both see and hear each other through a series of shared [Force visions](/wiki/Force_vision "Force vision"), despite being in two separate locations. At first, Rey swore to make Ren answer for his patricidal actions, although Ren was more intrigued by the connection they shared than Rey's threats. Unable to understand the act of killing one's own father, Rey assumed that Ren hated his father, but the dark-side warrior insisted that he did not hate Solo, causing Rey to beseech him for an explanation. He then revealed to the Jedi aspirant his desire to completely sever himself from the past, believing it was the only way to move forward and achieve his destiny.[[178]](#cite_note-Episode_VIII-178)

 [![Leia remembering a young Han Solo](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/44/WhatchaThinkinPrincess-PoeDameron27.png/revision/latest?cb=20190828042020) [![Leia remembering a young Han Solo](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/44/WhatchaThinkinPrincess-PoeDameron27.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20190828042020)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/44/WhatchaThinkinPrincess-PoeDameron27.png/revision/latest?cb=20190828042020) 

Leia remembering a young Han Solo

 

It was ultimately through their bond that Rey gained new insights into Ren, making her aware of the conflict between the dark side and the light within him. Unable to persuade Skywalker to end his self-imposed exile, she concluded that the son of Han Solo was the last hope of the galaxy, and therefore went directly to Ren in the hope of helping him find redemption in the light. Her arrival on the [First Order Navy](/wiki/First_Order_Navy "First Order Navy") [flagship](/wiki/Flagship "Flagship") *[Supremacy](/wiki/Supremacy "Supremacy")* provided Ren with an [opportunity](/wiki/Battle_of_Oetchi "Battle of Oetchi") to [assassinate](/wiki/Assassin "Assassin") his dark-side mentor, Supreme Leader Snoke. Although they worked together to kill Snoke's [Praetorian Guards](/wiki/Praetorian_Guard "Praetorian Guard"), Rey was dismayed to see that Ren did not intend to forsake his allegiance to the dark side. Instead, he invited her to rule the galaxy with him, bringing a new order to the galaxy. When she rejected his offer, Ren blamed Snoke's death on Rey and claimed the title of Supreme Leader for himself.[[178]](#cite_note-Episode_VIII-178)

When Skywalker later [projected](/wiki/Force_projection "Force projection") to the planet [Crait](/wiki/Crait "Crait") from Ahch-To in order to [confront](/wiki/Battle_of_Crait "Battle of Crait") Ren, he mentioned that Han would always be with him. Before succumbing to his projection, Skywalker's last words to Kylo were, "See you around, kid," remembering Solo even in the last seconds of his life.[[178]](#cite_note-Episode_VIII-178) After escaping from the First Order aboard the *Millennium Falcon*, both Organa and Chewbacca sat in the cockpit, where Organa remembered a young Solo sitting in the captain's seat, asking her what she was thinking. She then replied to Chewie that it was just echoes.[[180]](#cite_note-Poe_Dameron_27-180) Shortly afterwards, as BB-8 told R2-D2 his experiences at Starkiller Base, they discussed Solo's flying tactics, assuring that he was great.[[181]](#cite_note-Poe_Dameron_28-181) Later, when Leia tried to [convince](/wiki/Mission_to_the_Outer_Rim "Mission to the Outer Rim") the Mon Calamari to join their side as the First Order prepared to make an example of Mon Cala, Leia acknowledged that what she was asking them would require a kind of sacrifice as she had done several times over the years, silently remembering when she asked Han to go to Starkiller Base and meet their son only to be killed by Kylo in return.[[182]](#cite_note-Allegiance_4-182)

 [![In a Force vision, Ben Solo experiences the visage of Han, pleading for his son to renounce the dark side.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/38/BenSoloandHanSolo-TROS.png/revision/latest?cb=20230129165834) [![In a Force vision, Ben Solo experiences the visage of Han, pleading for his son to renounce the dark side.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/38/BenSoloandHanSolo-TROS.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/270?cb=20230129165834)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/38/BenSoloandHanSolo-TROS.png/revision/latest?cb=20230129165834) 

In a Force vision, Ben Solo experiences the visage of Han, pleading for his son to renounce the dark side.

 

[One year later](/wiki/35_ABY "35 ABY"), following Leia's death and his [own near death](/wiki/Mission_to_Kef_Bir "Mission to Kef Bir") at the [ruins of the second Death Star](/wiki/Death_Star_ruins "Death Star ruins"), Kylo experienced a Force vision that was a memory of Han on [Kef Bir](/wiki/Kef_Bir "Kef Bir"), who told his son that Kylo Ren was dead and that Ben Solo was alive. Kylo called Han just a memory, but Han told his son that he was his memory and urged Kylo to come home. Kylo felt it was too late as Leia was gone, but Han stated that while Leia was gone, what she stood for and fought for wasn't. Recalling their final interaction, Kylo admitted that he knew what he had to do but didn't know if he had the strength to do it. Han touched his son's face as he did after Kylo fatally stabbed him and assured his son that he did have the strength. Kylo once more drew his lightsaber, but after a moment turned around and threw it away, becoming Ben Solo once more. When Ben turned back around, Han had disappeared.[[174]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-174)

Shortly afterwards, while Poe was mourning Leia's death, he said that he wasn't ready to become the new leader of the Resistance. Lando, appeared and said that Luke, Han, Leia, and himself also weren't ready. When Poe asked how they defeated the Empire with nothing, he replied that they won because they had each other.[[174]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-174)

Later on, when Rey gave Ben the lightsaber that had once belonged to his grandfather, Ben saw that the [Knights of Ren](/wiki/Knights_of_Ren "Knights of Ren") were shocked and made the same gesture his father had made at the Battle of Endor: shrugging his shoulders.[[174]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-174)

## Personality and traits[]

### The smuggler turned general[]

:   "*Han fancied himself a scoundrel. But he wasn't. He loved freedom—for himself, certainly, but for everybody else in the galaxy, too. And time after time, he was willing to fight for that freedom. He didn't want to know the odds in that fight—because he'd already made up his mind that he'd prevail. And time after time, somehow, he did.*"
:   ―Leia Organa[[176]](#cite_note-The_Last_Jedi_Expanded_Edition-176)

 [![Solo developed a close friendship with Chewie.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/1f/Life-Day-MArvel-Issue-1-Noto-Cover-328s.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20210818090548) [![Solo developed a close friendship with Chewie.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/1f/Life-Day-MArvel-Issue-1-Noto-Cover-328s.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20210818090548)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/1f/Life-Day-MArvel-Issue-1-Noto-Cover-328s.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20210818090548) 

Solo developed a close friendship with Chewie.

 

Han Solo was a human male who stood at a height of 5 feet and 9 inches as a young adult, though eventually grew to a peak height of 6 feet and 1 inch, before shrinking down to 5 feet and 11 inches tall during his later years.[[183]](#cite_note-183) He had light skin, brown hair, and weighed 80 kilograms. Han was initially a cynical, disagreeable individual whose primary concern was gaining enough money to preserve his own life. He and Luke immediately disliked each other: Solo found Luke irritating and overly eager, and his open disdain for Kenobi's beliefs and actions did little to change Luke's initial view of Solo as an extortionist.[[6]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-6) During his younger, more selfish, days, he was willing to sacrifice a loved one when the situation called for it, as in the case of shooting Tobias Beckett to save himself despite considering him a mentor.[[9]](#cite_note-Solo-9) However, he came to change as he met Luke Skywalker and the Rebellion. After Han demonstrated his bravery on the Death Star and proved his loyalty, they became genuine friends, and soon after, Han became loyal to the Rebellion. Aside from his seemingly self-centered ways, Han was actually very loyal to his friends, and a good man.[[15]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-15) Having endured a difficult childhood as an impoverished orphan with no identity, Han instantly related to the Jakku scavenger Rey, who shared some of his skills.[[173]](#cite_note-TROSVD-173)

Solo enjoyed a good [Rodian Splice](/wiki/Rodian_Splice "Rodian Splice"),[[128]](#cite_note-SW_56-128) a drink typically ordered by, as described by the cook [Strono Tuggs](/wiki/Strono_Tuggs "Strono Tuggs"), "desperate" smugglers who wanted to prove something.[[184]](#cite_note-Cookbook-184) To Solo's annoyance, he found it hard to find an establishment that served a Rodian Splice that met his standards, which was complicated by how, if not brewed correctly, the drink would end up toxic. Forced to quickly flee a cantina during the Galactic Civil War, Solo expressed his annoyance at needing to leave without drinking a Rodian Splice that met his standards and sarcastically said they all could laugh about it later.[[128]](#cite_note-SW_56-128) Han's wife, Leia, described him as someone who had no patience for speeches or memorials, and was allergic to politics and suspicious of causes. However, according to Leia, he also hated bullies and could never stand down when confronted with them, and when he took on a difficult mission, he was never interested in knowing the odds of success.[[176]](#cite_note-The_Last_Jedi_Expanded_Edition-176) As Leia recognized, Han's first instinct was always to run when things got hard, but that he never ran far and always came back and stepped up again, knowing that there was a time to run and a time to make a stand.[[175]](#cite_note-Age_of_Resistance_Rey-175)

While most others regarded the ship as a piece of flying junk, Solo saw the *Millennium Falcon* as the embodiment of classic design, an opinion he shared with Chewbacca,[[185]](#cite_note-Insider230-185) and considered it his home.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4) Following the Battle of Endor, Han endeavored to honor Chewie's life debt to him by liberating the enslaved Wookiee homeworld from Imperial occupation.[[18]](#cite_note-Aftermath-18) Despite several setbacks, Han persisted with his mission. Together, Han and Chewie led a combined force of Wookiees, rebels, and mercenaries to spark a successful Wookiee uprising against the Empire. During the campaign, Han displayed resourcefulness and proved a cunning and effective commander. After the liberation of Kashyyyk, Han freed Chewbacca of his life debt so that he could reunite with his family.[[31]](#cite_note-Life_Debt-31)

 [![Han Solo, after acquiring the Millennium Falcon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/b4/HanSolo-SWOR.png/revision/latest?cb=20190208214553) [![Han Solo, after acquiring the Millennium Falcon](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/b4/HanSolo-SWOR.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20190208214553)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/b/b4/HanSolo-SWOR.png/revision/latest?cb=20190208214553) 

Han Solo, after acquiring the *Millennium Falcon*

 

Han Solo initially found the task of fatherhood challenging. While he envied Leia's Force connection to their son, Ben Solo, Han found that he had a special bond as a father.[[159]](#cite_note-Empire's_End-159) Due to their different interests and personalities, Solo and his wife lived separate lives. While she served as a New Republic senator, Solo managed a shipping company and organized starship races. Still, Solo kept in regular contact with his wife. On one occasion, he rescued Leia from a pro-Imperial militia known as the Amaxine warriors.[[19]](#cite_note-Bloodline-19)

Ben Solo's fall to the dark side of the Force had a profound impact on Han and Leia. Their marriage collapsed, and the two separated. With his shipping business floundering, Han resumed smuggling and incurred large debts with the criminal gangs Kanjiklub and the Guavian Death Gang. Solo regained his purpose when the scavenger Rey and the former stormtrooper Finn sought his help in smuggling the droid BB-8, who was carrying a [Map to Skywalker](/wiki/Map_to_Skywalker "Map to Skywalker"), to the Resistance. After reconciling with his wife, General Leia, Solo decided to try to bring his son back. Despite an emotional reunion between father and son, Kylo Ren killed his father. Han's death devastated Leia, Chewbacca, and Rey, who had come to view him as a father figure.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4) BB-8 would then remember Solo as a "maniac", to which R2-D2 clarified that Solo was "one of the best maniacs."[[181]](#cite_note-Poe_Dameron_28-181) Kylo himself would admit to being devastated by Han's death, telling Rey that he still loved his father.[[178]](#cite_note-Episode_VIII-178) After nearly dying, it would be a vision of Han that ultimately drove Ben back to the light side.[[174]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-174)

### Relationships[]

#### Qi'ra[]

:   "*I might be the only person who knows what you really are.*"
:   ―Qi'ra, to Han Solo — ![20?cb=20250116042720](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ee/Quote-audio.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/20?cb=20250116042720) [Link](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Qira-OnlyPerson.flac/revision/latest?cb=20250403184946)▶️ ([file info](/wiki/File:Qira-OnlyPerson.flac "File:Qira-OnlyPerson.flac"))[[9]](#cite_note-Solo-9)

 [![Solo kisses Qi'ra.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/66/QiraHanKiss-Solo.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230921121517) [![Solo kisses Qi'ra.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/66/QiraHanKiss-Solo.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20230921121517)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/66/QiraHanKiss-Solo.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230921121517) 

Solo kisses Qi'ra.

 

Solo met Qi'ra when they were scrumrats of the White Worms.[[9]](#cite_note-Solo-9) During one of their jobs, Solo and Qi'ra were forced to partner up. After Qi'ra was named Head, Solo and Qi'ra had dinner, which Solo believed was their first date.[[24]](#cite_note-Most_Wanted-24) Solo eventually fell in love with Qi'ra. The two made plans to buy a ship and run away together, although they never had the financial resources to do so until Solo stole unrefined coaxium from the White Worms. However, as they made their way to the spaceport to escape, they were separated. Despite Solo promising to come back for her, Qi'ra eventually joined Crimson Dawn. When the two reunited on the *First Light*, they rekindled their love for each other. Despite their feelings for each other, Qi'ra chose to stay in Crimson Dawn and leave Solo.[[9]](#cite_note-Solo-9)

#### Leia Organa[]

:   "*You have your moments. Not many of them, but you do have them.*"
:   ―Leia Organa, to Han Solo[[21]](#cite_note-Episode_V-21)

 [![Han Solo and Leia Organa](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2f/HanLeia-SWC.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220502220312) [![Han Solo and Leia Organa](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2f/HanLeia-SWC.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/225?cb=20220502220312)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2f/HanLeia-SWC.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220502220312) 

Han Solo and Leia Organa

 

When Solo and Organa first met, they got off to rough start, with Solo not responding well to Organa's attempts to order him around.[[6]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-6) The two of them eventually fell in love with each other during the [Galactic Civil War](/wiki/Galactic_Civil_War "Galactic Civil War") and shared their first kiss following the Battle of Hoth.[[21]](#cite_note-Episode_V-21) The two married after the war[[155]](#cite_note-Cross-155) and had a son, Ben Solo.[[159]](#cite_note-Empire's_End-159)

When Ben joined the First Order and became Kylo Ren, Solo and Organa, though married, separated to cope with their grief. When Han found himself pulled back into the fight, the two of them reunited briefly. Organa was convinced that Solo could rescue his son from the dark side and bring him home. When Solo was killed by their son, Organa sensed his death and cried for him.[[4]](#cite_note-Episode_VII-4) Organa continued to remember Solo[[180]](#cite_note-Poe_Dameron_27-180) and still believed he was the greatest pilot.[[181]](#cite_note-Poe_Dameron_28-181)

## Skills and abilities[]

:   "*Han is an incredible pilot. A decent mechanic too. He learns fast. And he already knows several languages. I can easily see him flying around the galaxy with his own ship someday.*"
:   ―Qi'ra[[24]](#cite_note-Most_Wanted-24)

 [![Han Solo was known throughout the galaxy as one of its best pilots.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d5/Han_Solo_ME.png/revision/latest?cb=20170727030638) [![Han Solo was known throughout the galaxy as one of its best pilots.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d5/Han_Solo_ME.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20170727030638)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d5/Han_Solo_ME.png/revision/latest?cb=20170727030638) 

Han Solo was known throughout the galaxy as one of its best pilots.

 

Since his earliest days of running scams on the streets of Corellia, Han had already exhibited traits that would later serve to solidify his prodigious piloting skills. Solo's apparent proficiency of getting out of difficult situations served the smuggler well, a trait notably exhibited during Solo's [famed Kessel Run](/wiki/Raid_on_Kessel "Raid on Kessel"), which the young [spacer](/wiki/Spacer "Spacer") completed in just over twelve [parsecs](/wiki/Parsec "Parsec").[[9]](#cite_note-Solo-9) In an unprecedented display of expert flying, Han had navigated through the notoriously treacherous [Akkadese Maelstrom](/wiki/Akkadese_Maelstrom "Akkadese Maelstrom"), reviled for its reputation of representing certain doom for ill-fated starships that dared to tempt fate.[[32]](#cite_note-Solo_Comic_7-32) Solo's innate instinct for piloting propelled the up-and-coming outlaw into the forefront of the criminal underworld, eventually catching the eye of the infamous [gangster](/wiki/Gangster "Gangster") Jabba the Hutt, who employed the young Han as his premier [spice](/wiki/Spice "Spice") smuggler. During the [reign](/wiki/Imperial_Era "Imperial Era") of the Galactic Empire, Jabba's [criminal syndicate](/wiki/Jabba%27s_criminal_empire "Jabba's criminal empire") flourished, thanks in large part to *Millennium Falcon*'s speed and capable crew. Solo and his loyal [first mate](/wiki/First_Mate "First Mate") Chewbacca performed several smuggling runs under the employ of Jabba, proving time and time again that the duo carried enormous financial potential. Han was trained as a cadet in the Imperial Academy before and after being reassigned to [224th Imperial Armored Division](/wiki/224th_Imperial_Armored_Division "224th Imperial Armored Division") in [Mimban](/wiki/Mimban "Mimban"), displaying his proficiency as a soldier despite his insubordination and reckless behavior, Han once noted that in order to survive, he needs to fight dirty in order to win as he uses his brawling skills,[[27]](#cite_note-Imperial_Cadet_1-27)[[15]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-15) he was known for his marksmanship to the point he was able to "quick draw" his blaster to shoot first.[[9]](#cite_note-Solo-9)

 [![Solo was an excellent shot with a blaster even into his senior years.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9a/HanSoloTFA-SWBC25.png/revision/latest?cb=20231231050938) [![Solo was an excellent shot with a blaster even into his senior years.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9a/HanSoloTFA-SWBC25.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20231231050938)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9a/HanSoloTFA-SWBC25.png/revision/latest?cb=20231231050938) 

Solo was an excellent shot with a blaster even into his senior years.

 

Shortly after his fateful encounter with the Jedi Master Obi-Wan Kenobi and young [farmhand](/wiki/Moisture_farmer "Moisture farmer") [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker"),[[6]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-6) Solo rose to become a prominent member of the Rebel Alliance. Solo displayed his natural leadership acumen in several missions, eventually convincing the Alliance to offer the former smuggler a commission within the Rebellion's military. In time, Solo came to accept the commission.[[74]](#cite_note-Complete_VD-74) To that end, Captain Han Solo spearheaded several Alliance operations, utilizing the *Millennium Falcon*'s speed and firepower to great effect in the ongoing plight against the Empire. By the time of the Battle of Endor, Solo had elevated to the rank of General within the [Rebel Army](/wiki/Alliance_Army "Alliance Army"), further demonstrating his leadership skills on the [forested moon](/wiki/Endor "Endor") of [Endor](/wiki/Endor_(planet) "Endor (planet)"). Solo led the successful ground assault on the land-based [shield generator](/wiki/SLD-26_planetary_shield_generator "SLD-26 planetary shield generator") of the second Death Star, during which he and Rebel [Pathfinders](/wiki/Special_Forces_Trackers_Unit "Special Forces Trackers Unit") detonate several [detonite charges](/wiki/Detonite_charge "Detonite charge") which disabled the deflector shield surrounding the battle station, thus allowing the Rebel fleet to commence its attack on the Death Star's main reactor.[[15]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-15)

## Behind the scenes[]

### Origins and development[]

:   "*You old stardog. Took a war to get you out here…*"
:   ―Han Solo's opening line in the rough draft of *The Star Wars*[[186]](#cite_note-rough_draft-186)

 [![Harrison Ford and his co-stars relax on the set of Star Wars.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6c/Relaxingontheset-MOSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20131104062553) [![Harrison Ford and his co-stars relax on the set of Star Wars.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6c/Relaxingontheset-MOSW.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20131104062553)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6c/Relaxingontheset-MOSW.png/revision/latest?cb=20131104062553) 

Harrison Ford and his co-stars relax on the set of *Star Wars*.

 

Han Solo was created by [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas") during the development of Lucas' [1977](/wiki/1977 "1977") film, [*Star Wars*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope") and is present in Lucas' 132-page [*The Star Wars: Rough Draft*](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_rough_draft "The Star Wars rough draft"), completed in [May](/wiki/May "May") [1974](/wiki/1974 "1974"). In the draft, Solo is a [Ureallian](/wiki/Yourellian "Yourellian"), and is described as a "huge green-skinned monster with no nose and large gills". He is a member of the Jedi Bendu and an old friend of General Skywalker.[[186]](#cite_note-rough_draft-186) As Lucas refined his story, Solo evolved into a burly, bearded, flamboyantly dressed pirate.[[187]](#cite_note-db-187) Although Lucas had originally intended for Solo to be a nefarious alien character, he settled on the idea of a human so that he could develop more of a relationship between the film's three primary characters. Chewbacca thus filled the role of the alien sidekick.[[188]](#cite_note-characters-188) By [August](/wiki/August "August") [1975](/wiki/1975 "1975"), when Lucas had written his [third draft](/wiki/Adventures_of_the_Starkiller,_Episode_I:_The_Star_Wars "Adventures of the Starkiller, Episode I: The Star Wars"), Solo was described as "A tough [James Dean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Dean "wikipedia:James Dean") style starpilot about twenty-five years old. A [cowboy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cowboy#Popular_culture "wikipedia:Cowboy") in a starship -- simple, sentimental, and cocksure of himself."[[189]](#cite_note-third_draft-189) This incarnation of Solo's character went on to appear in the finished film.[[6]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-6)[[187]](#cite_note-db-187)

While developing Solo's character, Lucas defined him in relation to the film's hero, Luke Skywalker. Selflessness was an important theme throughout the film, and Skywalker was a selfless young idealist. Lucas thought of Solo as the sidekick with contrary morals to the hero, and wrote him as a selfish character.[[188]](#cite_note-characters-188) [Harrison Ford](/wiki/Harrison_Ford "Harrison Ford"), who portrayed Solo in all three films of *[Star Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars "Star Wars")*'s [original trilogy](/wiki/Original_trilogy "Original trilogy"), has described Solo as the smart-ass to Skywalker's callow youth, with each character having had a clear section of turf to explore.[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190)

[Michael Arndt](/wiki/Michael_Arndt "Michael Arndt") developed Kylo Ren as a convincing means to have Han and Leia separate after *Return of the Jedi*. However, it was not decided to kill off the character until [J.J. Abrams](/wiki/J.J._Abrams "J.J. Abrams") felt, "'What is Han doing in this movie?' If we're not going to have something important and irreversible happen to him, then he kind of feels like luggage. He feels like this great, sexy piece of luggage you have in your movie. But he's not really evolving. He's not really pushing the story forward." Abrams decided killing off Han meant the character's son had a chance of becoming a worthy successor to Darth Vader.[[191]](#cite_note-ew-191)

On [May 5](/wiki/May_5 "May 5"), [2016](/wiki/2016 "2016"), it was announced that [Alden Ehrenreich](/wiki/Alden_Ehrenreich "Alden Ehrenreich") would be playing the character in the [spinoff film](/wiki/Solo:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Solo: A Star Wars Story").[[192]](#cite_note-Cast-192)

### Portrayal[]

:   "*I thought that the luck of the character was that he represented something close to the audience's sensibilities because of his distance and resistance to the mythology.*"
:   ―Harrison Ford[[193]](#cite_note-30years-193)

When casting the role of Solo, Lucas sought actors who had individual screen presence as well as chemistry with Skywalker. He wanted Solo to be older than Skywalker and to possess a cynical edge. Lucas desired new and unknown actors to play *Star Wars*'s major roles, and originally forbade Harrison Ford from auditioning, having worked with him on the [1973](/wiki/1973 "1973") film [*American Graffiti*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Graffiti "wikipedia:American Graffiti").[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190) Ford was working as a carpenter on the set of the auditions,[[194]](#cite_note-60mins-194)[[193]](#cite_note-30years-193) and was brought in by Lucas to feed lines to the actors who were auditioning,[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190) including [Kurt Russell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_Russell "wikipedia:Kurt Russell"), [Nick Nolte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Nolte "wikipedia:Nick Nolte"), [Christopher Walken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Walken "wikipedia:Christopher Walken"),[[187]](#cite_note-db-187) and [Perry King](/wiki/Perry_King "Perry King"). While feeding lines, Ford impressed Lucas by giving the character a mix of mercenary swagger and world weariness, and convinced the director to let him play the part.[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190)

 [![Alden Ehrenreich was cast to play a young Han in Solo: A Star Wars Story.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2e/HanSolo-SoloOMG.png/revision/latest?cb=20231103010741) [![Alden Ehrenreich was cast to play a young Han in Solo: A Star Wars Story.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2e/HanSolo-SoloOMG.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20231103010741)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/2/2e/HanSolo-SoloOMG.png/revision/latest?cb=20231103010741) 

Alden Ehrenreich was cast to play a young Han in *Solo: A Star Wars Story*.

 

Ford went on to portray Solo in both of *Star Wars*'s sequels, [1980](/wiki/1980 "1980")'s [*The Empire Strikes Back*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_V_The_Empire_Strikes_Back "Star Wars: Episode V The Empire Strikes Back") and [1983](/wiki/1983 "1983")'s [*Return of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VI_Return_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi"), as well as [1978](/wiki/1978 "1978")'s *[The Star Wars Holiday Special](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Holiday_Special "The Star Wars Holiday Special")*.[[195]](#cite_note-Holiday_Special-195) He was hesitant to sign the contracts for the sequels, however, feeling that Solo's character should be killed off.[[196]](#cite_note-q&a-196) When Lucas was discussing the script of *Return of the Jedi* with director [Richard Marquand](/wiki/Richard_Marquand "Richard Marquand") and screenwriter [Lawrence Kasdan](/wiki/Lawrence_Kasdan "Lawrence Kasdan"), the three were unsure if Ford would return for the film. Solo's character had been frozen in carbonite during the climax of *The Empire Strikes Back*, and Ford was a rising star in Hollywood following his starring role as [Indiana Jones](/wiki/Indiana_Jones "Indiana Jones") in [1981](/wiki/1981 "1981")'s [*Raiders of the Lost Ark*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raiders_of_the_Lost_Ark "wikipedia:Raiders of the Lost Ark"). Ford himself thought that Solo should die in *Jedi*, sacrificing himself to save Skywalker and Princess Leia. He reasoned that Solo had no family, future or responsibilities to the story,[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190) and that his death would give the story some resonance.[[196]](#cite_note-q&a-196) Kasdan also believed that a major character death early in *Jedi* would keep audiences worried, believing that none of the characters were safe. Lucas vetoed the idea, however, and Solo ultimately survived.[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190)

The script of *The Empire Strikes Back* originally called for Solo to respond to Princess Leia's declaration of "I love you" with "I love you too." Ford disliked the line, feeling that the established character of Solo wasn't being taken advantage of. After many takes, director [Irvin Kershner](/wiki/Irvin_Kershner "Irvin Kershner") wasn't satisfied either. He told Ford not to think about it, and to say whatever he thought that Solo would say. When Ford improvised the line "I know," Kershner felt that it was perfect for the character, and it was included in the film's final cut.[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190) Solo's carbonite block was created out of a mold sourced from both Ford and Bossk actor [Alan Harris](/wiki/Alan_Harris "Alan Harris"), who provided the mold for the neck down. Ford only provided the mold for Solo's face, secured via a molding compound applied by makeup designer [Stuart Freeborn](/wiki/Stuart_Freeborn "Stuart Freeborn"). As put by *[Star Wars Insider](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider "Star Wars Insider")*, Ford "gamely endured" the molding process.[[197]](#cite_note-226_Archive-197)

Harrison Ford has referred to Solo as an inherently relatable character to audiences, owing to his separation from the overarching mythological themes of the saga.[[193]](#cite_note-30years-193) However, he saw Solo as a chess piece that could be moved around and even killed, as the character wasn't as important to *Star Wars* as its Force-using characters.[[196]](#cite_note-q&a-196) Ford has called Solo a thin character,[[198]](#cite_note-starpulse-198)[[199]](#cite_note-babs-199) and one that wasn't interesting enough to be developed throughout several sequels, unlike Indiana Jones.[[196]](#cite_note-q&a-196)[[199]](#cite_note-babs-199) As such, Ford thought that if Solo died in *Return of the Jedi*, it would introduce a needed complication for the character and give the story resonance.[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190)[[196]](#cite_note-q&a-196)[[198]](#cite_note-starpulse-198)

In the animated microseries *[Star Wars Forces of Destiny](/wiki/Star_Wars_Forces_of_Destiny "Star Wars Forces of Destiny")*, the younger and older Han Solo are respectively voiced by [AJ LoCascio](/wiki/AJ_LoCascio "AJ LoCascio") and [Kiff VandenHeuvel](/wiki/Kiff_VandenHeuvel "Kiff VandenHeuvel"). Voice actor [Lex Lang](/wiki/Lex_Lang "Lex Lang") voiced Han Solo for the game *Battlefront II*, having voiced Solo as well in a previous game.[[200]](#cite_note-Rogue_Squadron_III-200)

### Rejected and unused concepts[]

:   "*I found part of a transmitter droid near the east bay... I think it's still sending and receiving signals.*"
:   ―Han Solo's line from the rough draft of [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith")[[201]](#cite_note-making-201)

 [![Concept art of a young Han Solo, originally set to appear in Revenge of the Sith](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/07/YoungHanConcept-MakingOfROTS.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20190412061318) [![Concept art of a young Han Solo, originally set to appear in Revenge of the Sith](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/07/YoungHanConcept-MakingOfROTS.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/225?cb=20190412061318)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/07/YoungHanConcept-MakingOfROTS.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20190412061318) 

Concept art of a young Han Solo, originally set to appear in *Revenge of the Sith*

 

Several unused concepts and shots of Solo exist within *Star Wars* film lore. The scene that sees Luke Skywalker, Obi-Wan Kenobi, and the viewer first meet Solo and Chewbacca in the original film was at one point set to feature Solo sitting with and kissing a woman named Jenny.[[190]](#cite_note-dreams-190)[[202]](#cite_note-jenny-202) A young Han Solo was slated to appear on Kashyyyk in [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005")'s [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), living among the planet's Wookiees as well as assisting [Yoda](/wiki/Yoda "Yoda"). No actor was cast, and the character was cut from the final draft.[[201]](#cite_note-making-201)[[203]](#cite_note-art-203) However, the concept was somewhat recycled with [Jaybo Hood](/wiki/Jaybo_Hood "Jaybo Hood") in the *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* episode "[Mystery of a Thousand Moons](/wiki/Mystery_of_a_Thousand_Moons "Mystery of a Thousand Moons")." George Lucas placed off-limits the possibility of using Han Solo in *The Clone Wars* when writer [Henry Gilroy](/wiki/Henry_Gilroy "Henry Gilroy") was writing the show bible,[[204]](#cite_note-The_Force_Filoni_Gilroy-204) a restriction that was maintained until the show's cancellation.

While developing the story of [*Star Wars*: Episode VII *The Force Awakens*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VII_The_Force_Awakens "Star Wars: Episode VII The Force Awakens"), after director J.J. Abrams decided to kill off Solo in the film's climax, it was discussed how to show Kylo Ren stabbing Solo with his lightsaber. One proposal was to show Kylo stabbing Solo in front of the abyss just when he was getting his blaster from its holster, falling to his demise like in the finished version of the film. This idea, however, was ultimately cut.[[205]](#cite_note-TLJ_concept_art-205)

In the [Star Wars Resistance](/wiki/Star_Wars_Resistance "Star Wars Resistance") episode "[The Platform Classic](/wiki/The_Platform_Classic "The Platform Classic")," Han Solo was originally scripted to appear in the episode, but the creators decided to focus on [Jarek Yeager](/wiki/Jarek_Yeager "Jarek Yeager")'s character instead so [Marcus Speedstar](/wiki/Marcus_Speedstar "Marcus Speedstar") replaced Han in the episode.[[206]](#cite_note-Bucket's_List-206)

### Return to the films and death[]

Before reprising the role for *Star Wars*: Episode VII *The Force Awakens*, Ford indicated that he was unlikely to portray Solo again.[[199]](#cite_note-babs-199)[[207]](#cite_note-mtv-207) When asked if Ford was sad when they finally killed off the character, director J.J. Abrams replied, "Nah, he was fine." Describing filming the scene, he said, "It was really chilling. Seeing these two actors [Ford and [Adam Driver](/wiki/Adam_Driver "Adam Driver")], they weren't chewing up the scenery. They were just doing this thing in a way that, frankly, was disturbing. To see Harrison reach out and touch Adam. I know this sounds stupid, but literally watching it, I forgot — I forgot that he wasn't his son. He did it so beautifully."[[191]](#cite_note-ew-191) Despite the character's death, Ford commented, "I'm finished with *Star Wars* if *Star Wars* is finished with me. [...] I can't imagine [being asked back]. But it is science fiction."[[208]](#cite_note-Solo_Done-208) Nevertheless, Ford reprised the role as a Force vision in the [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019") film [*Star Wars*: Episode IX *The Rise of Skywalker*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IX_The_Rise_of_Skywalker "Star Wars: Episode IX The Rise of Skywalker"), although he was uncredited.[[174]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-174) Some fans interpreted Solo's appearance to actually be the man himself, appearing somehow from beyond death, instead of simply being a vision or memory.[[209]](#cite_note-Ford_Shocked-209)

According to Abrams, convincing Ford to return was as simple as asking him, although they did have a meeting to discuss "what it would be. Harrison, who is one of the great people ever, and incredibly thoughtful about everything that he does, all he ever wants is to understand the utility of the character. 'What is my role?' It was about sitting with him and explaining what our intention was. We talked about it for quite a while, I sent him the pages. He got it, and of course, as you can see, he was wonderful."[[210]](#cite_note-Vanity_far-210) Ford stated he was surprised to return to *Star Wars* given his character's death but took the opportunity after Abrams promised it would be "great." Ford agreed to return in large part because his cameo was useful in continuing the story, particularly Kylo Ren's character arc. He was also pleased to have a chance to work with Adam Driver again. When asked about the fan discussion as to whether Solo had somehow returned from the grave for the scene, such as as a Force ghost, Ford remarked that he had no idea what a Force ghost was.[[209]](#cite_note-Ford_Shocked-209)

### Impact on popular culture[]

:   ![Blue Glass Arrow](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D) *See also: [Han shot first](/wiki/Han_shot_first "Han shot first")*

:   "*Han Solo is that character that we always wished we could be. I think most of us felt like Luke Skywalker, but we would have loved to have been Han Solo.*"
:   ―[Peter Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Jackson "wikipedia:Peter Jackson"), director of [*The Lord of the Rings* film trilogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_trilogy "wikipedia:The Lord of the Rings film trilogy")[[188]](#cite_note-characters-188)

In 2005, Solo placed #14 on the list of [greatest film heroes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years%E2%80%A6100_Heroes_and_Villains "wikipedia:AFI's 100 Years…100 Heroes and Villains") composed by the [American Film Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Film_Institute "wikipedia:American Film Institute").[[211]](#cite_note-afi_1-211) The criteria involved in the list's selection included cultural impact, legacy, and inspiration to contemporary artists and audiences, and heroism defined as prevailing in extreme circumstances coupled with a sense of morality, courage, and purpose.[[212]](#cite_note-afi_2-212) [Empire magazine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_(magazine) "wikipedia:Empire (magazine)") deemed Solo the fourth greatest movie character of all time, citing him as full of charm and laconic cool that was brought by Harrison Ford.[[213]](#cite_note-empiremag-213) The magazine [*Entertainment Weekly*](/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly_Books "Entertainment Weekly Books") ranked him #7 on their list of the all-time coolest heroes in pop culture,[[214]](#cite_note-weekly-214) and the website Fandomania.com placed him at #15 on their [2009](/wiki/2009 "2009") list of the 100 greatest fictional characters.[[215]](#cite_note-fandomania-215)

 [![George Lucas sporting a "Han shot first" t-shirt on the set of Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/79/Kelly_and_George.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070902054422) [![George Lucas sporting a "Han shot first" t-shirt on the set of Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/79/Kelly_and_George.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20070902054422)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/7/79/Kelly_and_George.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070902054422) 

George Lucas sporting a "Han shot first" t-shirt on the set of *Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull*

 

The developers of the [2008](/wiki/2008 "2008") video game [*Prince of Persia*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_of_Persia_(2008_video_game) "wikipedia:Prince of Persia (2008 video game)") cited both Solo and Indiana Jones as having inspired their nameless protagonist.[[216]](#cite_note-persia-216) Actor [Chris Pine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Pine "wikipedia:Chris Pine") also named both characters as sources he drew upon when preparing to play [James T. Kirk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_T._Kirk "wikipedia:James T. Kirk") in the 2009 film [*Star Trek*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Trek_(film) "wikipedia:Star Trek (film)"), mentioning their humor and "accidental hero" traits.[[217]](#cite_note-kirk-217)

Solo's likeness has been used in a variety of media, including the American television shows [*Mind of Mencia*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind_of_Mencia "wikipedia:Mind of Mencia") and [*Robot Chicken*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robot_Chicken "wikipedia:Robot Chicken").[[218]](#cite_note-Robot_Chicken-218) In the cartoon [*Family Guy*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_Guy "wikipedia:Family Guy")'s *Star Wars*–themed episodes "[Blue Harvest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Harvest "wikipedia:Blue Harvest")," "[Something, Something, Something, Dark Side](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Something,_Something,_Something,_Dark_Side "wikipedia:Something, Something, Something, Dark Side")," and "[It's a Trap!](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/It%27s_a_Trap! "wikipedia:It's a Trap!")," the character [Peter Griffin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Griffin "wikipedia:Peter Griffin") plays the role of Solo.[[219]](#cite_note-Blue_Harvest-219), [Mel Brooks'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mel_Brooks "wikipedia:Mel Brooks") [1987](/wiki/1987 "1987") *Star Wars* spoof [*Spaceballs*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spaceballs "wikipedia:Spaceballs") features a protagonist named Lone Starr, who parodies both Solo and Skywalker.[[220]](#cite_note-spaceballs-220)[[221]](#cite_note-spaceballs2-221)

When George Lucas made a slight edit to one of Solo's scenes for the [1997](/wiki/1997 "1997") [Special Edition](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Trilogy_Special_Edition "The Star Wars Trilogy Special Edition") of the original *Star Wars* film, the change and its consequent fan response developed into somewhat of a pop-culture meme.[[222]](#cite_note-shootfirst-222)[[223]](#cite_note-thinkgeek-223) The original version of the film depicted Solo shooting the bounty hunter Greedo before Greedo could fire a shot of his own,[[6]](#cite_note-Episode_IV-6) but the Special Edition added in a laser blast from Greedo that preceded Solo's shot but harmlessly hit the wall.[[224]](#cite_note-special-224) Many fans disapproved of the change, and an online petition that called for Lucas to re-release the original cut of the scene was signed by thousands.[[225]](#cite_note-petition-225)[[226]](#cite_note-10otherthings-226) T-shirts were produced reading "Han Shot First,"[[223]](#cite_note-thinkgeek-223) and Lucas was even spotted wearing one on the set of the 2008 film [*Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indiana_Jones_and_the_Kingdom_of_the_Crystal_Skull "wikipedia:Indiana Jones and the Kingdom of the Crystal Skull").[[227]](#cite_note-lucasshirt-227)

Arguments over the subject appear in the films [*Jay and Silent Bob Strike Back*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jay_and_Silent_Bob_Strike_Back "wikipedia:Jay and Silent Bob Strike Back") and [*Clerks II*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clerks_II "wikipedia:Clerks II"),[[228]](#cite_note-jay&bob-228)[[229]](#cite_note-clerksii-229) and a scene from the 2005 movie [*Serenity*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serenity_(film) "wikipedia:Serenity (film)") was inspired by the debate.[[230]](#cite_note-serenity-230) When [the original versions](/wiki/Original_unaltered_trilogy "Original unaltered trilogy") of the *Star Wars* trilogy were released on DVD in [2006](/wiki/2006 "2006"), a promotional article on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") stated that fans could "yes, see Han Solo shoot first."[[231]](#cite_note-lucassays-231)

Readers of Empire magazine voted Han Solo the greatest *Star Wars* character in 2018.[[232]](#cite_note-Han_Solo_Voted_Greatest_Star_Wars_Character_By_Empire_Readers-232)

### Continuity[]

"[Scorched](/wiki/Scorched "Scorched")," set in [21 ABY](/wiki/21_ABY "21 ABY"),[[2]](#cite_note-Timelines-2) depicts Han Solo with his [hair](/wiki/Hair "Hair") already [graying](/wiki/Color "Color"),[[165]](#cite_note-Scorched-165) as does the comic story "[Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon](/wiki/Flight_of_the_Falcon,_Part_5:_Grand_Theft_Falcon "Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon")."[[168]](#cite_note-Adventures_18-168) However in "[Maz's Scoundrels](/wiki/Maz%27s_Scoundrels "Maz's Scoundrels")," which is set between these stories,[[233]](#cite_note-Maz's_Scountrels-233) Han's hair is still brown.[[234]](#cite_note-Scoundrels-234) Han's hair is also is also brown in [*Life Day* 1](/wiki/Life_Day_1 "Life Day 1"), set after "Grand Theft Falcon,"[[235]](#cite_note-Life_Day-235) and returns to gray in [*Poe Dameron Annual* 2](/wiki/Poe_Dameron_Annual_2 "Poe Dameron Annual 2").[[170]](#cite_note-PD_annual_2-170)

### Ambiguous canon[]

In the [2015](/wiki/2015 "2015") novel *[Battlefront: Twilight Company](/wiki/Battlefront:_Twilight_Company "Battlefront: Twilight Company")*, there is a scene where the rebel soldier [Hazram Namir](/wiki/Hazram_Namir "Hazram Namir") encounters an unnamed captain making repairs to his ship in Echo Base.[[236]](#cite_note-Twilight_Company-236) The book's author, [Alexander Freed](/wiki/Alexander_Freed "Alexander Freed"), later strongly implied on Twitter that the captain was intended to be Han Solo.[[237]](#cite_note-Freed_Tweet-237) The scene plays out as follows:

One day, a Rebel captain worked on repairs to his freighter in Echo Base's main hangar when a young rebel soldier who looked like he'd been through a beating walked under the captain's ship lugging a canister of [bacta](/wiki/Bacta "Bacta"). Curious, he asked the rebel what had happened to him. The trooper, [First Sergeant](/wiki/First_Sergeant "First Sergeant") Hazram Namir of the [61st Mobile Infantry](/wiki/61st_Mobile_Infantry "61st Mobile Infantry"), cynically replied that he had gotten into a fistfight with an overzealous and patriotic member of the Alliance Special Forces. The captain just smiled and went back to his work. Later that evening, Namir—though the captain never got the man's name, and he never gave his—boarded the *Falcon* with a bin of mechanical parts with orders to give them to the captain on behalf of the Alliance deck crew. He began installing the parts, and asked Namir whom he had gotten into a fight with, to which Namir told him he had fought a man named [Kryndal](/wiki/Kryndal "Kryndal"). Namir assisted the captain in repairing the ship for over thirty minutes, and when the captain finished—or maybe just gave up—he produced a bottle of [Corellian whiskey](/wiki/Corellian_whiskey "Corellian whiskey"), and the two shared several drinks while Namir explained how he had ended up on cargo duty, and the captain how his freighter had been damaged. He identified with Namir, so he admitted that he was something like a mercenary, and hadn't joined the Rebellion because he believed in their cause. Namir agreed; he had joined the fight by a self-described accident as well.[[236]](#cite_note-Twilight_Company-236)

Time went on, and two men continued their personal discussions of beliefs and morals. The captain expressed his worry with the future state of galactic government—if the Alliance eventually conquered the Empire as they so hoped, men like him and Namir, who didn't believe in the Rebellion's cause, would be shunted once smugglers and mercenaries weren't required for the Alliance to operate. Namir wholeheartedly agreed, and secretly hoped the Galactic Civil War would go on forever. The captain took one last sip of the [whiskey](/wiki/Whiskey "Whiskey"), handed the bottle to Namir, and continued the repairs. Namir, too, went back on his business.[[236]](#cite_note-Twilight_Company-236)

[↑](#cite_ref-SW_25_Date_161-0) [Premium-Era-real](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0e/Premium-Era-real.png/revision/latest?cb=20241019125517) [Marvel's New Star Wars Series to Explore the New Republic Erae](https://www.ign.com/articles/marvels-new-star-wars-series-to-explore-the-new-republic-era) by Schedeen, Jessie on [IGN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IGN "wikipedia:IGN") ([January 21](/wiki/January_21 "January 21"), [2025](/wiki/2025 "2025")) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20250121171444/https://www.ign.com/articles/marvels-new-star-wars-series-to-explore-the-new-republic-era) archived on [January 21](/wiki/January_21 "January 21"), [2025](/wiki/2025 "2025")) states the events of [*Star Wars*](/wiki/Star_Wars_(2025) "Star Wars (2025)") begin around two [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the events of [*Star Wars*: Episode VI *Return of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VI_Return_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi"), which *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates to [4 ABY](/wiki/4_ABY "4 ABY"). 162. [↑](#cite_ref-Ahsoka_Date_162-0) [SWInsider](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider "Star Wars Insider") "[A Certain Point of View](/wiki/A_Certain_Point_of_View_(department) "A Certain Point of View (department)")" — [*Star Wars Insider* 228](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_228 "Star Wars Insider 228") dates the events of "[Part Seven: Dreams and Madness](/wiki/Part_Seven:_Dreams_and_Madness "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness")" to nine [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"), which corresponds to [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY") per *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")*. Preceding episodes, also take place in that year, since they take place after *[Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Book_of_Boba_Fett "Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett")*, which is dated to 9 [ABY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system") according to *Timelines*. As "[Part Eight: The Jedi, the Witch, and the Warlord](/wiki/Part_Eight:_The_Jedi,_the_Witch,_and_the_Warlord "Part Eight: The Jedi, the Witch, and the Warlord")" takes place shortly after Part Seven, the events of [*Ahsoka*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka") as a whole must all take place within the same year. 163. [↑](#cite_ref-Part_Six_163-0) [AhsokaTitle-Template](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka") *[Star Wars: Ahsoka](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka")* — "[Part Six: Far, Far Away](/wiki/Part_Six:_Far,_Far_Away "Part Six: Far, Far Away")" 164. [↑](#cite_ref-The_Rise_of_Kylo_Ren_2_166-0) [*The Rise of Kylo Ren* 2](/wiki/The_Rise_of_Kylo_Ren_2 "The Rise of Kylo Ren 2") 167. [↑](#cite_ref-Kylo_didn't_know_he_was_Vader's_heir_167-0) [Claudia Gray](/wiki/Claudia_Gray "Claudia Gray")'s novel [*Bloodline*](/wiki/Bloodline_(novel) "Bloodline (novel)") clarifies that Ben was ignorant of his grand-parentage until [Ransolm Casterfo](/wiki/Ransolm_Casterfo "Ransolm Casterfo")'s revelation in the [Galactic Senate](/wiki/New_Republic_Senate "New Republic Senate") 168. ↑ [168.0](#cite_ref-Adventures_18_168-0) [168.1](#cite_ref-Adventures_18_168-1) [168.2](#cite_ref-Adventures_18_168-2) [IDWStarWarsAdventuresLogoSmaller](/wiki/Star_Wars_Adventures_(2017) "Star Wars Adventures (2017)") "[Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon](/wiki/Flight_of_the_Falcon,_Part_5:_Grand_Theft_Falcon "Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon")" — [*Star Wars Adventures* (2017) 18](/wiki/Star_Wars_Adventures_(2017)_18 "Star Wars Adventures (2017) 18") 169. ↑ [169.0](#cite_ref-Date1_169-0) [169.1](#cite_ref-Date1_169-1) "Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon" takes place after the events of "[The Crimson Corsair and the Lost Treasure of Count Dooku](/wiki/The_Crimson_Corsair_and_the_Lost_Treasure_of_Count_Dooku "The Crimson Corsair and the Lost Treasure of Count Dooku")," as [Kix](/wiki/Kix "Kix") is indirectly mentioned, but before [*Life Day* 1](/wiki/Life_Day_1 "Life Day 1"), which *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates to c. [31 ABY](/wiki/31_ABY "31 ABY"). "The Crimson Corsair and the Lost Treasure of Count Dooku" refers to the prologue as taking place 50 [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") prior to the main story. The prologue takes place in between "[The Wrong Jedi](/wiki/The_Wrong_Jedi "The Wrong Jedi")" and [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), both of which are placed in [19 ABY](/wiki/19_ABY "19 ABY") by *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")*. Therefore the prologue takes place in 19 [BBY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system"), and the main story takes place around 31 ABY. Therefore, "Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon" also takes place around 31 ABY. 170. ↑ [170.0](#cite_ref-PD_annual_2_170-0) [170.1](#cite_ref-PD_annual_2_170-1) [*Poe Dameron Annual* 2](/wiki/Poe_Dameron_Annual_2 "Poe Dameron Annual 2") 171. ↑ [171.0](#cite_ref-Smuggler's_Guide_171-0) [171.1](#cite_ref-Smuggler's_Guide_171-1) [171.2](#cite_ref-Smuggler's_Guide_171-2) *[Star Wars: Smuggler's Guide](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Smuggler%27s_Guide "Star Wars: Smuggler's Guide")* 172. [↑](#cite_ref-Han_Solo_Voted_Greatest_Star_Wars_Character_By_Empire_Readers_232-0) [Premium-Era-real](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0e/Premium-Era-real.png/revision/latest?cb=20241019125517) [Han Solo Voted Greatest Star Wars Character By Empire Readers](https://www.empireonline.com/movies/news/han-solo-voted-greatest-star-wars-character-empire-readers) on [www.empireonline.com](https://www.empireonline.com) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20250515134950/https://www.empireonline.com/movies/news/han-solo-voted-greatest-star-wars-character-empire-readers) archived on [May 15](/wiki/May_15 "May 15"), [2025](/wiki/2025 "2025")) 233. [↑](#cite_ref-Maz's_Scountrels_233-0) "Maz's Scoundrels" depicts [Han Solo](/wiki/Han_Solo/Legends "Han Solo/Legends") and [Chewbacca](/wiki/Chewbacca "Chewbacca") in possession of the *[Millennium Falcon](/wiki/Millennium_Falcon "Millennium Falcon")*, therefore meaning it must take place before they lose it in "[Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon](/wiki/Flight_of_the_Falcon,_Part_5:_Grand_Theft_Falcon "Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon")." Furthermore, *[Star Wars Encyclopedia: The Comprehensive Guide to the Star Wars Galaxy](/wiki/Star_Wars_Encyclopedia:_The_Comprehensive_Guide_to_the_Star_Wars_Galaxy "Star Wars Encyclopedia: The Comprehensive Guide to the Star Wars Galaxy")* establishes the events of "Maz's Scoundrels" are set after Solo and Chewbacca returned to [smuggling](/wiki/Smuggler "Smuggler") following the former's separation from [Leia Organa](/wiki/Leia_Skywalker_Organa_Solo "Leia Skywalker Organa Solo"), which *Timelines* dates to around [29 ABY](/wiki/29_ABY "29 ABY"). *Timelines* also dates "[Scorched](/wiki/Scorched "Scorched")" to [21 ABY](/wiki/21_ABY "21 ABY") Therefore, the events of "Maz's Scoundrels" must occur between "Scorched" and "Flight of the Falcon, Part 5: Grand Theft Falcon." 234. [↑](#cite_ref-Scoundrels_234-0) "[Maz's Scoundrels](/wiki/Maz%27s_Scoundrels "Maz's Scoundrels")" — [*Age of Resistance Special* 1](/wiki/Age_of_Resistance_Special_1 "Age of Resistance Special 1") 235. [↑](#cite_ref-Life_Day_235-0) [*Life Day* 1](/wiki/Life_Day_1 "Life Day 1") 236. ↑ [236.0](#cite_ref-Twilight_Company_236-0) [236.1](#cite_ref-Twilight_Company_236-1) [236.2](#cite_ref-Twilight_Company_236-2) *[Battlefront: Twilight Company](/wiki/Battlefront:_Twilight_Company "Battlefront: Twilight Company")* 237. [↑](#cite_ref-Freed_Tweet_237-0) [TwitterLogo](https://twitter.com) [Alexander Freed](/wiki/Alexander_Freed "Alexander Freed") ([@AlexanderMFreed](https://twitter.com/AlexanderMFreed)) on [Twitter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter "wikipedia:Twitter") ([post](https://twitter.com/AlexanderMFreed/status/847241572609544194)): "I'm allowed, but if readers (or another writer!) interpret it differently, I don't mind. Do I think it's him? Yeah, I do!" ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20191016092542/https://twitter.com/AlexanderMFreed/status/847241572609544194)) ([screenshot](/wiki/File:Twilight_Company_Han.png "File:Twilight Company Han.png")) |
